Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Understand and compare CAD technologies with traditional methods of designing, focusing on 
advantages such as efficiency, precision, and cost-effectiveness 
2. Explore different topologies of CAD systems, including design databases, graphic standards, and 
data exchange formats, and understand their role in facilitating efficient design processes 
3. Acquire practical skills in 2D graphics algorithms, transformations and grasp fundamental concepts 
in 3D graphic 
 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Evolution of CAD/CAM and CIM, Industrial Look at CAD, Comparison of 
CAD with traditional designing, Application of Computers in Design. 
 Topologies of CAD systems- Design database, graphic Standards, data 
Exchange Formats, virtual Reality.  
2D graphics: Line drawing algorithms, DDA line algorithm – Circle 
drawing, Bressnham’s circle drawing algorithm- 2D transformation: 
translation, rotation, scaling, reflection, clipping – 3D graphics basics  
Shigley Modelling in CAD

system in CIM. Introduction to Rapid prototyping 
Robot technology: Basic Components- Sensors and Actuators- Robot 
application in Automotive Industry 
 
Suggestion: -Task project- Students can choose their focus areas such as –  
CIM, OSI, JIT and GT, Virtual Reality

SEMESTER S5 
MECHATRONICS AND CONTROL SYSTEMS 
Course Code 
PCAUT521 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week (L: 
T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. 
To impart knowledge on mechatronic systems, data presentation, and control mechanisms using 
sensors, transducers, and activation systems 
2. 
To impart knowledge on signal conditioning, input/output systems, and electromechanical 
devices, emphasizing practical mechatronic design and fault-finding solutions 
3. 
To understand control systems engineering, including automatic control concepts, system 
representation, transfer functions, block diagrams, and practical control applications 
4. 
To understand system response, control system analysis, frequency response, and stability 
criteria using techniques like Bode plots and root locus 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Mechatronics: 
Systems-Microprocessor 
based 
controllers 
- 
mechatronic approach - sensors - transducers - force - velocity 
displacement - temperature 
Data presentation systems: Displays - measurement systems -
calibration - pneumatic and hydraulic systems - control valves - 
actuators - mechanical and electrical activation systems-relays and 
solenoid switches - proximity pickups. 
 
9 
2 
Signal Conditioning: Signal conditioning - operational amplifiers - 
filtering – multiplexers 
Input/output Systems:  Ports, interface requirements, adaptors -
programmable logic controllers - data handling digital communications 
- system, networks, protocols, interfaces, fault finding - design and 
 
9 

 
 
mechatronic design solutions. Electromechanical systems: CD, DVD 
Rom, OCR, Printers 
3 
Introduction to Control Systems Engineering: Concept of automatic 
control - open loop and closed loop systems - transfer functions - 
Representation of control components and systems -Translational and 
rotational mechanical components – series and parallel combinations - 
Block diagrams - comparators, integrating devices, Servomechanisms, 
hydraulic servomotors, temperature control systems, speed control 
systems. 
9 
4 
System Response: First and second order system - Response to step, 
pulse, ramp and sinusoidal input-systems with distance, velocity lag. 
Control System Analysis: Transient Response of simple control 
systems - Stability of control systems - Routh Stability criteria - Error 
Analysis. 
Frequency Response Analysis: Polar plots - Experimental 
determination of frequency response - Bode plot and Nyquist stability 
criteria - Gain and phase margin. Root locus of simple transfer function.
 
9

SEMESTER S5 
AUTOMOTIVE POLLUTION AND TESTING 
Course Code 
PEAUT522 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand pollutant sources, formation mechanisms, environmental impacts, and 
compliance with international emission standards. 
2. To demonstrate proficiency in analyzing the formation of pollutants like NOx, CO, 
particles, and hydrocarbons in engines, and applying emission measurement procedures 
for vehicles. 
3. Apply knowledge of emission control technologies in gasoline and diesel vehicles, 
evaluate inspection procedures, and assess vehicle replacement and retrofit programs 
to meet emission standards.  
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction: Pollutants – sources – formation – effects of pollution on 
environment – human. Emission standards & regulations –International 
standards, US, European union standards, & Indian standards. Compliance 
with standards – certification - assembly lane testing – In use surveillance & 
recall. 
 
9 
2 
Mechanism of pollutant formation – Formation of NOx & CO in SI and CI 
engines – formation of particles in SI and CI engines – oxidation of soot – role 
of soot inhibitors Formation of HC – aldehydes, ketones, alcohols, and organic 
acids - formation of HC in SI and Diesel Engines. Non-Exhaust Emissions -
Emission measurement and testing procedures – light and heavy-duty vehicles 
& two wheelers. Crankcase, evaporative, refuelling and on-road emissions. 
NDIR analysers, FID, Chemiluminescence analysers etc. 
 
9 

 
 
3 
Technology for controlling emissions – Gasoline fuelled vehicles – A/F ratio, 
electronic control. Catalytic convertors – two way and three way convertors – 
catalytic wear and poisoning. Diesel fuelled vehicles – engine design – exhaust 
after treatment – Particulate trap  EGR- Crankcase emission and control - 
evaporative emission and control – fuel dispensing and distribution emissions 
and control, SCR, diesel oxidation catalyst (DOC) Diesel Exhaust Fluid 
(DEF), 
9 
4 
Controlling emission - inspection procedures for SI engines – exhaust & 
evaporative emissions – motorcycle white smoke. Institutional setting for 
inspection and maintenance – centralized and decentralized I/M – comparison 
– inspection frequency and roadside inspection Vehicle replacement and 
retrofit programs – scrap age and relocation – replacement – retrofit program. 
9

Course Objectives:

thermodynamics, cycle efficiency, and types of refrigerants used. 
2. Understand and classify various air conditioning systems, components, and their operational 
principles, focusing on their layout and impact on automotive and building environments. 
3. Understand and optimize air distribution systems, including duct sizing, ventilation, and control 
mechanisms. 
4. Develop proficiency in diagnosing, servicing, and maintaining air conditioning systems. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Principles of refrigeration: Thermodynamics of refrigeration Carnot, reversed 
Carnot cycle, heat pump, and refrigerator- coefficient of performance -unit of 
refrigeration. Refrigeration methods-conventional refrigeration systems. Air 
refrigeration system –Bell Coleman cycle -C.O.P –capacity, types of 
refrigerants.  
 
9 
2 
Air Conditioning Systems - Classification, layouts, central, unitary air 
conditioning 
systems, 
components 
like 
compressors, 
evaporators, 
condensers, expansion devices, fan blowers, heating systems, Automotive 
heaters, Types, Heater Systems, Air conditioning protection, Engine 
protection. 
Load Analysis: Outside & inside design consideration, factors 
forming the load on refrigeration & air conditioning systems, procedure for 
cooling & heating load calculation in automobiles, effect of air conditioning 
load on engine performance. 
 
9 

 
 
3 
Air Distribution Systems: Distribution duct system, sizing, supply and 
return ducts, type of grills, diffusers, ventilation, air noise level, layout of 
duct systems for automobiles. 
  
Air Routing & Temperature Control: Objectives, evaporator air flow 
through the recirculating unit, automatic temperature control, duct system, 
controlling flow, vacuum reserve, testing the air control of air handling 
systems. 
Air Conditioning Control: Common control such as thermostats, humidistat, 
control dampers, pressure cut outs, relays 
9 
4 
Air conditioning service: Air conditioner maintenance & service- causes of 
air conditioner failure, leak testing guide, discharging the system. Evacuating 
the system, charging the system, servicing heater system, removing & 
replacing components, trouble shooting of air conditioning system, 
compressor service, methods of dehydration, charging & testing. 
 
9

SEMESTER S5 
OPERATIONS MANAGEMENT IN AUTO INDUSTRY 
Course Code 
PEAUT524 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To provide students with a comprehensive understanding of the fundamental concepts of 
production and operations management specifically tailored to the automotive industry. 
2. To equip students with the skills to strategically plan production activities in automotive 
manufacturing. 
3. To enable students to analyse and manage supply chain operations, apply quality management 
principles and environmental sustainability practices to enhance efficiency and competitiveness 
in the automotive sector. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to Production and Operations Management, production vs. 
productivity, the importance of productivity, factors affecting productivity, 
methods to improve productivity. 
Work Study: Method Study, Time Study, Importance, Techniques of Work 
Measurement, Procedure of Conducting. Labour efficiency, methods to 
improve labour productivity, manpower planning - factors affecting, steps 
involved, fatigue – causes and remedies, motivation, methods to motivate 
employees. 
 
9 
2 
Strategic Planning of Production Activities, Industrial Development, and Life 
Cycle of a Product. 
Make or Buy Decision Making: Factors Influencing Make or Buy Decision. 
Manufacturing Systems Adopted in Car Manufacturing, Overview of 
Technologies for Materials Applied to the Construction of Vehicles, General 
Guidelines for Setting Product Design for Automotive Products, Automotive 
 
9 

 
 
Industrialization Process Description, Product Data Management (PDM), 
PDM Analysis, Product Breakdown Structure (PBS), Bill of Material 
(BOM). 
3 
Supply Chain Management: Objectives, Elements of the Supply Chain, 
Drivers, Activities, Process View of a Supply Chain, Flows in SCM, Factors 
to be Considered for Developing a Supply Chain, Basic Requirements for 
Successful SCM, Supply Chain Structure in Automotive Industries. 
Challenges and Strategies in a Globalized Automotive Market. Key 
Performance Indicators of Logistics. 
Production Planning: Forecasting, Capacity Planning, and Aggregate 
Production Planning. 
Inventory Management: JIT (Just-In-Time) and Lean Principles in 
Automotive Manufacturing. 
9 
4 
Quality Management: Total Quality Management (TQM), Six Sigma, and 
Their Application in Auto Production. 
Advanced Manufacturing Technologies: Robotics, Automation, IoT (Internet 
of Things), and AI (Artificial Intelligence) Applications in Automotive 
Operations. 
Innovation in Product Development: Design for Manufacturing (DFM), 
Concurrent Engineering, and Prototyping. 
Environmental Sustainability: Green Manufacturing Practices and 
Regulations in the Auto Industry. 
 
9

SEMESTER S5 
ELECTRIC DRIVES AND CONTROLS FOR AUTOMATION 
Course Code 
PEAUT525 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
5/3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Comprehend the principles of operation, emf equations, and characteristics of shunt and series 
excited DC generators and motors, along with their torque-speed equations and industry 
applications. 
2. Understand the principles of transformer operations, including emf equations, vector diagrams, 
and efficiency calculations, by conducting and interpreting OC and SC tests. 
3. Understand the operation principles of single-phase motors and synchronous machines, 
including their types, regulation methods, and starting mechanisms. 
4. Study the operation and control methods of stepper motors and gain insights into various 
automation controllers, such as servo controls, digital controllers, and programmable logic 
controllers. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
DC Machines-principle of operation-emf equation-shunt and series 
excited DC generators. General idea of armature reaction, OCC and 
load characteristics 
Principles of series and shunt DC motors-torque and speed equations-
torque speed characteristics- Applications of dc shunt series and 
compound motors. Principles of starting. 
 
9 

 
 
2 
Transformers – principles of operations – emf equation-vector 
diagrams- losses and efficiency – OC and SC tests. Equivalent circuits- 
efficiency calculations- maximum efficiency 
 
9 
3 
Single phase motors- principle of operation of single-phase induction 
motor – split phase motor – capacitor start motor- 
Synchronous machines types – emf equation of alternator – regulation 
of alternator by emf method. Principles of operation of synchronous 
motors- methods of starting. 
9 
4 
Stepper motors: Principle of operation, variable reluctance motors, 
Hybrid stepper motors, Linear stepper motor, comparison, Torque-
speed characteristics, control of stepper motors 
Controllers for automation- servo control, Digital controllers, motor 
controllers, Axis controllers, Machine tool controllers, Programmable 
Logic Controllers 
 
9

Course Objectives: 
1. To provide students with hands-on experience in inspecting, servicing on various electrical 
circuits associated with automobiles. 
2. To equip students with the practical skills necessary for diagnosing, maintaining, and 
adjusting electrical components such as lights, alternator, battery, starter motor, compressor 
and battery.

using advanced technological systems for electrical systems.

Continuous Assessment (25 Marks) 
1. Preparation and Pre-Lab Work (7 Marks) 
 Pre-Lab Assignments: Assessment of pre-lab assignments or quizzes that test understanding 
of the upcoming experiment. 
 Understanding of Theory: Evaluation based on students’ preparation and understanding of 
the theoretical background related to the experiments. 
2. Conduct of Experiments (7 Marks) 
 Procedure and Execution: Adherence to correct procedures, accurate execution of 
experiments, and following safety protocols. 
 Skill Proficiency: Proficiency in handling equipment, accuracy in observations, and 
troubleshooting skills during the experiments. 
 Teamwork: Collaboration and participation in group experiments. 
3. Lab Reports and Record Keeping (6 Marks) 
 Quality of Reports: Clarity, completeness and accuracy of lab reports. Proper documentation 
of experiments, data analysis and conclusions. 
 Timely Submission: Adhering to deadlines for submitting lab reports/rough record and 
maintaining a well-organized fair record. 
 
4. Viva Voce (5 Marks) 
 Oral Examination: Ability to explain the experiment, results and underlying principles 
during a viva voce session. 
Final Marks Averaging: The final marks for preparation, conduct of experiments, viva, and 
record are the average of all the specified experiments in the syllabus. 
Evaluation Pattern for End Semester Examination (50 Marks) 
1. Procedure/Preliminary Work/Design/Algorithm (10 Marks) 
 Procedure Understanding and Description: Clarity in explaining the procedure and 
understanding each step involved. 
 Preliminary Work and Planning: Thoroughness in planning and organizing 
materials/equipment. 

 
 
 Algorithm Development: Correctness and efficiency of the algorithm related to the 
experiment. 
 Creativity and logic in algorithm or experimental design. 
 
2. Conduct of Experiment/Execution of Work/Programming (15 Marks) 
 Setup and Execution: Proper setup and accurate execution of the experiment or programming 
task. 
3. Result with Valid Inference/Quality of Output (10 Marks) 
 Accuracy of Results: Precision and correctness of the obtained results. 
 Analysis and Interpretation: Validity of inferences drawn from the experiment or quality of 
program output. 
 
4. Viva Voce (10 Marks) 
 Ability to explain the experiment, procedure results and answer related questions 
 Proficiency in answering questions related to theoretical and practical aspects of the subject. 
 
5. Record (5 Marks) 
 Completeness, clarity, and accuracy of the lab record submitted

Video Links (NPTEL, SWAYAM…) 
 
Link ID 
 
Computer-Aided Design- 
https://nptel.ac.in/translation 
 
Continuous Assessment (25 Marks) 
1. Preparation and Pre-Lab Work (7 Marks) 
 Pre-Lab Assignments: Assessment of pre-lab assignments or quizzes that test understanding 
of the upcoming experiment. 
 Understanding of Theory: Evaluation based on students’ preparation and understanding of 
the theoretical background related to the experiments. 
2. Conduct of Experiments (7 Marks) 
 Procedure and Execution: Adherence to correct procedures, accurate execution of 
experiments, and following safety protocols. 
 Skill Proficiency: Proficiency in handling equipment, accuracy in observations, and 
troubleshooting skills during the experiments. 
 Teamwork: Collaboration and participation in group experiments. 
3. Lab Reports and Record Keeping (6 Marks) 
 Quality of Reports: Clarity, completeness and accuracy of lab reports. Proper documentation 
of experiments, data analysis and conclusions. 
 Timely Submission: Adhering to deadlines for submitting lab reports/rough record and 
maintaining a well-organized fair record. 
 
 

 
 
4. Viva Voce (5 Marks) 
 Oral Examination: Ability to explain the experiment, results and underlying principles 
during a viva voce session. 
Final Marks Averaging: The final marks for preparation, conduct of experiments, viva, and 
record are the average of all the specified experiments in the syllabus. 
Evaluation Pattern for End Semester Examination (50 Marks) 
1. Procedure/Preliminary Work/Design/Algorithm (10 Marks) 
 Procedure Understanding and Description: Clarity in explaining the procedure and 
understanding each step involved. 
 Preliminary Work and Planning: Thoroughness in planning and organizing 
materials/equipment. 
 Algorithm Development: Correctness and efficiency of the algorithm related to the 
experiment. 
 Creativity and logic in algorithm or experimental design. 
 
2. Conduct of Experiment/Execution of Work/Programming (15 Marks) 
 Setup and Execution: Proper setup and accurate execution of the experiment or programming 
task. 
3. Result with Valid Inference/Quality of Output (10 Marks) 
 Accuracy of Results: Precision and correctness of the obtained results. 
 Analysis and Interpretation: Validity of inferences drawn from the experiment or quality of 
program output. 
4. Viva Voce (10 Marks) 
 Ability to explain the experiment, procedure results and answer related questions 
 Proficiency in answering questions related to theoretical and practical aspects of the subject. 
5. Record (5 Marks) 
 Completeness, clarity, and accuracy of the lab record submitted

SEMESTER S6 
HYBRID AND FUEL CELL VEHICLES 
Course Code 
PCAUT601 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:1:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
4 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None  
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Understand the fundamental principles and components of hybrid and fuel cell vehicle 
technologies, including their energy conversion mechanisms and powertrain configurations.
 
 
2. Understand the environmental and societal impacts of hybrid and fuel cell vehicles, comparing 
their advantages and challenges with conventional internal combustion engine vehicles. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to hybrid electric vehicles: Need for hybrid and electric 
vehicles, components, advantages and disadvantages, application, social and 
environmental impacts. Hybrid Electric Drive-trains: Basic concept of hybrid 
traction, introduction to various hybrid drive-train topologies (Series, Parallel, 
Series – Parallel), power flow control in hybrid drive-train topologies. 
 
11 
2 
Electric Machines and their controllers: ‘Brushed’ DC Electric Motor - 
DC regulation and voltage conversion; Brushless Electric Motors - Brushless 
DC motor, Switched reluctance motors, Induction motor; Motor cooling, 
efficiency, size and mass. Thermal Management of HEV Power Electronics 
Sizing the drive system: Matching the electric machine and the internal 
combustion engine (ICE), 
 
11 
3 
Energy Storage: Introduction to Energy Storage Requirements in Hybrid and 
Electric Vehicles, Battery based energy storage and its analysis, Super 
Capacitor based energy storage and its analysis, Ultra capacitors, Flywheel 
based 
energy 
storage 
and 
its 
analysis, 
Flywheel 
Accumulators, 
Superconducting magnetic energy storage; Hydraulic Accumulators; 
Hydraulic Pumps/Motors - Pneumatic Hybrid Engine Systems. Energy 
11 

 
 
management strategies used in hybrid and electric vehicles: types, comparison 
and implementation issues Hybridization of different energy storage devices 
4 
Fuel cell:  Fuel Cell based energy storage and its analysis characteristics, 
types: alkaline fuel cell. Proton exchange Membrane; direct methanol fuel cell. 
Phosphoric acid fuel cell, molten carbonate fuel cell, solid oxide fuel cell, 
Hydrogen storage systems - reformers; Fuel cell vehicles.  
 
11

SEMESTER S6 
VEHICLE STABILITY AND DYNAMICS 
Course Code 
PCAUT602 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Understand the performance characteristics and vibration behaviour of road vehicles, including 
the effects of tractive resistance, tractive effort, and power requirements 
2. Comprehend the dynamics of tires and braking systems, focusing on tire behaviour during 
cornering, braking dynamics, and the impact of tire characteristics on vehicle performance 
3. Analyze the stability of vehicles under various conditions, considering load distribution, 
gyroscopic effects, and the impact of aerodynamic forces on road loads and vehicle handling 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Performance of road vehicles: Tractive resistance, tractive effort, power 
required for propulsion, grade ability, drawbar pull and the problems 
related to these terms. 
Road performance curves- acceleration, grad ability and drawbar pull. 
Vibrations-Free vibrations of single degree freedom systems, energy 
method. Undamped and damped free vibrations, viscous damping, 
critical 
damping, 
logarithmic 
decrement 
(Numericals 
only) 
transmissibility. Vehicle Vibration and human comforts 
 
9 
2 
Tires: tire dynamics Ride characteristics, Behavior while Cornering, 
Slip angle, Cornering force, Power consumed by Tire, Over steer, 
under steer, steady state cornering, aligning moment-combined 
braking and Cornering, effect of camber & transient effects in 
cornering. Tire Vibrations. 
Braking Dynamics: Braking     requirements, stopping distance, 
 
9 

 
 
braking efficiency, work done in braking, tire adhesion. 
3 
Stability of vehicles: Load distribution (Three wheeled and four 
wheeled vehicles), Calculation of acceleration, tractive effort and 
reactions for different drives, stability of a vehicle on a curved track, 
slope and a banked road. 
Gyroscopic effects, weight transfer during acceleration, Cornering and 
braking, cross wind handling. 
9 
4 
Road Loads: Air resistance-Mechanics of air flow around a vehicle, 
pressure distribution on a vehicle, factors affecting rolling resistance, 
aerodynamic forces – aerodynamic drag, drag components, drag 
coefficient, aerodynamic aids, aerodynamic side force, lift force, 
pitching moment, yawing moment, rolling moment, cross wind 
sensitivity 
 
9

SEMESTER S6 
TWO AND THREE WHEELED VEHICLES 
Course Code 
PEAUT631 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0

60

2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
NA 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Learn about different types of two and three-wheelers, including their design, 
suspension, steering, and powertrain technologies. 
2. Gain skills in analysing transmission, drive systems, braking mechanisms, and 
components of electric vehicles. 
3. Develop proficiency in vehicle maintenance, safety standards, and emerging 
technologies in vehicle design and smart systems. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Two and Three Wheelers: Types of two and three-wheelers. Frame 
and chassis design. Suspension systems. Steering systems 
Powertrain and Engine Technology: Types of engines (two-stroke 
and four-stroke). Engine components and functions. Fuel systems and 
carburettors. 
 
9 
2 
Transmission Systems: Types of transmissions (manual, automatic, 
and CVT). Clutch systems and operation. Gearbox and gear ratios 
Drive Systems: Chain, belt, and shaft drives. Differentials and final 
drive. 
Braking Systems: Braking systems (drum and disc brakes).  
 
9 
3 
Electric Two and Three Wheelers: Battery types, Battery Chargers, 
Charging Port Specifications. Types of electric motors used in two and 
three-wheel vehicles, Battery Management Systems, Motor Controllers. 
9 

 
 
4 
Vehicle Maintenance: Routine maintenance and servicing. Common 
troubleshooting and repair techniques 
Safety Systems and Regulations: Retrofitting of IC engines to EV in 
two/three wheelers. Safety standards and regulations. Rider safety gear 
and ergonomics 
Emerging Technologies: Advanced materials and lightweight 
construction. Smart and connected vehicle technologies. 
 
9

SEMESTER S6 
AUTONOMOUS DRIVING AND ADAS 
Course Code 
PEAUT632 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand the principles and components of autonomous driving and ADAS technologies. 
2. To explore the various sensor technologies and their integration into autonomous and ADAS 
systems. 
3. To analyse the role of AI, machine learning, and software platforms in autonomous driving. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Fundamentals of Autonomous Driving - Levels of vehicle autonomy 
(SAE levels 0-5), Key components of autonomous vehicles , Overview 
of autonomous vehicle architectures  
Advanced Driver Assistance Systems (ADAS) Overview - Definition 
and objectives of ADAS, Key ADAS features: Lane keeping assist, 
adaptive cruise control, automated parking, Benefits and challenges of 
ADAS 
Vehicle Communication and Networking - In-vehicle networking 
(CAN, LIN, FlexRay), Vehicle-to-everything (V2X) communication , 
Role of wireless technology in autonomous driving.  
Regulatory and Ethical Considerations- Legal aspects of autonomous 
driving , Ethical considerations and safety standards 
Current regulations and future trends 
 
9 
2 
Radar and Lidar Systems - Basics of radar technology, Applications 
and limitations of radar in vehicles, Fundamentals of Lidar technology, 
 
9 

 
 
Lidar applications in 3D mapping and obstacle detection 
Camera Systems and Image Processing - Types of cameras used in 
ADAS , Image processing techniques for vehicle safety, Night vision 
technology and applications. 
Ultrasonic and Infrared Sensors - Principles of ultrasonic sensor 
operation, Applications in parking assist and obstacle detection 
Infrared sensors and their role in ADAS 
Sensor Data Fusion - Introduction to sensor data fusion, Techniques for 
combining data from different sensors, Benefits of sensor fusion in 
enhancing system accuracy and reliability 
3 
Artificial Intelligence and Machine Learning - Role of AI in 
autonomous vehicles , Machine learning algorithms for vehicle 
perception and decision-making, Deep learning applications in 
autonomous driving. 
Autonomous Driving Platforms and Software - Overview of 
autonomous driving software architectures, Key platforms: ROS (Robot 
Operating System), Autoware, Apollo, Software development and 
simulation tools. 
Path Planning and Control Systems - Fundamentals of path planning 
algorithms, Control systems for vehicle stability and navigation, Real-
time decision-making, and obstacle avoidance 
Cloud Computing and Edge Processing - Role of cloud computing in 
autonomous vehicle ecosystems, Edge processing for real-time data 
handling, Examples of cloud-based autonomous driving platforms 
9 
4 
System Integration and Calibration - Integration of ADAS components 
into vehicle systems, Calibration techniques for sensors and actuators, 
Challenges in system integration 
Testing and Validation - Testing methodologies for autonomous and 
ADAS systems, Simulation environments and test tracks, Validation 
processes and safety assessments 
Maintenance and Troubleshooting - Common issues in ADAS and 
autonomous systems, Diagnostic tools and software, Maintenance best 
practices for autonomous vehicles 
 
9 

 
 
Case Studies and Future Trends- Case studies of leading autonomous 
vehicle projects, Emerging trends in autonomous driving and ADAS 
technology, Future directions and research opportunities

SEMESTER S6 
VEHICLE TRANSPORT AND FLEET MANAGEMENT 
Course Code 
PEAUT633 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
NA 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To provide a comprehensive understanding of the principles and practices of vehicle 
transport and fleet management. 
2. To equip students with the skills necessary to manage and optimize fleet operations, 
including maintenance, fuel management, and safety compliance. 
3. To introduce advanced technologies and strategic planning techniques used in modern 
fleet management to enhance efficiency and sustainability. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Fundamentals of Vehicle Transport - Overview of vehicle transport 
systems, Types of transport vehicles (commercial, public, private), Role 
of vehicle transport in the economy 
Fleet Management Basics - Definition and scope of fleet management, 
Objectives and importance of fleet management, Components of fleet 
management systems 
Vehicle Acquisition and Leasing - Methods of vehicle acquisition 
(purchase, lease, hire), Cost-benefit analysis of different acquisition 
methods, Fleet financing options      
Vehicle Life Cycle Management - Phases of vehicle life cycle, 
Strategies for extending vehicle life, Disposal and resale of vehicles 
 
9 
2 
Fleet Operations - Fleet scheduling and routing, Trip planning and 
management, Driver management and training  
 
9 

 
 
Vehicle Maintenance Management - Preventive vs. corrective 
maintenance. Maintenance scheduling and record keeping. Use of 
telematics in maintenance 
Fuel Management - Fuel procurement and storage , Fuel consumption 
monitoring , Strategies for reducing fuel costs 
Safety and Compliance - Regulatory requirements for fleet operations, 
Safety management systems, Accident management and reporting 
3 
Fleet Management Software - Types of fleet management software, 
Features and functionalities, Benefits of using fleet management 
software 
Telematics and GPS Tracking - Introduction to telematics, GPS 
tracking systems and their applications, Benefits of telematics in fleet 
management 
Data Analytics in Fleet Management - Importance of data analytics , 
Key performance indicators (KPIs) for fleets Using data for decision 
making  
Automation and Future Trends - Electric and hybrid vehicles in 
fleets, Autonomous vehicles in fleet management, Emerging trends in 
fleet management technology, case studies.  
9 
4 
Fleet Planning and Optimization - Strategic fleet planning, Fleet 
optimization techniques, Route optimization and load planning 
Cost Management in Fleet Operations - Cost components of fleet 
management, Cost control strategies, Budgeting, and financial planning 
for fleets 
Environmental Considerations - Environmental impact of fleets, 
Strategies 
for reducing environmental footprint, 
green 
fleet 
management practices 
Case Studies and Best Practices - Analysis of successful fleet 
management practices, Case studies of leading fleet operations, Lessons 
learned and best practices in fleet management 
 
9

SEMESTER S6 
VEHICLE MAINTENANCE 
Course Code 
PEAUT635 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
5/3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To provide a comprehensive understanding of vehicle maintenance principles and practices for 
conventional, electric, and hybrid vehicles. 
2. To equip students with practical skills for diagnosing, servicing, and maintaining various 
vehicle systems and components. 
3. To familiarize students with advanced diagnostic tools, safety practices, and emerging trends 
in vehicle maintenance technology. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to Vehicle Maintenance - Importance and objectives of 
vehicle maintenance, Types of maintenance: Preventive, predictive, and 
corrective, Preparation of maintenance schedules and checklists, 
Record keeping and documentation 
Advanced Diagnostics - Use of advanced diagnostic tools and 
software, Common sensor errors and rectification methods, Emerging 
trends in vehicle maintenance technology 
Safety in Vehicle Maintenance - General safety guidelines, 
Use of personal protective equipment (PPE), Tool safety and safe 
handling of hazardous materials 
 
9 
2 
Engine Maintenance - Routine maintenance of petrol and diesel 
engines, Scheduled maintenance services for different operating 
conditions, Inspection and replacement of drive belts, spark plugs, and 
valve adjustments, Cooling and lubrication systems maintenance 
 
9 

 
 
Transmission Maintenance - Types of transmissions: Manual, 
automatic, AMT, CVT, DSG , Common problems and maintenance 
procedures , Clutch maintenance: Inspection, adjustment, and 
replacement , Gearbox maintenance: Inspection, adjustment, and repair
Brake  Maintenance - Types of brake systems: Hydraulic, mechanical, 
ABS, Brake inspection, cleaning, adjustment, and replacement, Brake 
bleeding procedures , Troubleshooting common brake issues 
3 
Body and Chassis Maintenance - Body repair tools and techniques: 
Tinkering, painting, soldering, and metalloid paste application, Tyre 
and wheel maintenance: Rotation, balancing, and alignment , 
Suspension system: Service, repair, and overhauling , Steering system: 
Service, repair, and overhauling Electrical System Maintenance - 
Battery maintenance: Inspection, testing, and replacement , Charging 
and starting system maintenance , Lighting system maintenance , 
Electrical wiring and connector inspection and repair 
9 
4 
Electric Vehicle (EV) Maintenance - Introduction to electric vehicles 
and their components, Routine and scheduled maintenance of EVs, 
Maintenance of high voltage battery, motor, inverter, On-Board 
Charger (OBC), and reduction gear, Safety precautions in handling high 
voltage systems 
Hybrid Vehicle Maintenance - Introduction to hybrid vehicles and 
their components, Maintenance of hybrid drive systems: Engine, 
electric motor, battery, and control systems 
Inspection 
and 
servicing 
of 
regenerative 
braking 
systems, 
Troubleshooting common hybrid vehicle issues 
 
 
9

SEMESTER S6 
AUTOMOTIVE COMPONENT DESIGN 
Course Code 
PBAUT604 
CIE Marks 
60 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:1 
ESE Marks 
40 
Credits 
4 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To Understand the fundamentals of design, including the design process, preferred numbers, 
standards, codes, and material properties, and their behaviour under various stresses. 
2. To Analyse different theories of failure, shock and impact loads, fatigue loading, and factors 
affecting endurance limits and safety. 
3. To Design mechanical components such as shafts, bearings, springs, gears, clutches, brakes, 
and internal combustion engine parts, considering their material properties, loading conditions, 
and failure mechanisms. 
4. To Apply principles of lubrication, bearing selection, gear design, and the impact of static and 
dynamic loads on mechanical systems to ensure efficient and reliable performance. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to Design- Definition, steps in design process, preferred 
numbers, standards, and codes in design. Materials and their properties- 
Elastic and plastic behaviour of metals, ductile and brittle behaviour, 
shear, bending and torsional stresses, combined stresses, stress 
concentration factor. 
Theories of Failure- Guest’s Theory, Rankine’s Theory, St. Venant’s 
Theory, Haigh’s Theory, and Von Mises and Hencky Theory. Shock 
and impact loads, fatigue loading, endurance limit stress, factors 
affecting endurance limit, factor of safety. 
 
9 

 
 
Shafting- material, design considerations, causes of failure in shafts, 
design based on strength, rigidity and critical speed, design for static 
and fatigue loads, repeated loading, reversed bending. 
Suggestions-problem project- Students can explore innovative 
approaches to design processes, integrating preferred numbers, 
standards, and codes into practical design solutions. 
2 
Rolling contact bearing- Design of bearings, Types, Selection of a 
bearing type, bearing life, static and dynamic load capacity, axial and 
radial loads, selection of bearings, dynamic equivalent load. Sliding 
contact bearing- lubrication, lubricants, viscosity, Journal bearings, 
hydrodynamic theory, Sommer field number, design considerations. 
Springs- classification, spring materials, stresses and deflection of 
helical springs, axial loading, curvature effect, resilience, static and 
fatigue loading, surging, critical frequency, end construction. Leaf 
springs- Flat springs, semi elliptical laminated leaf springs, design of 
leaf springs. 
Suggestion-problem project -students will have the autonomy to 
explore and design bearing and spring systems based on specified 
performance criteria and real-world applications. The project will 
integrate concepts from rolling contact bearings, sliding contact 
bearings, and springs, focusing on design considerations, material 
selection, and performance analysis. 
 
 
9 
3 
Gears- classification, Gear nomenclature, Tooth profiles, Materials of 
gears, Law of gearing (review only), virtual or formative number of 
teeth, gear tooth failures, Beam strength, Lewis equation, 
Buckingham’s equation for dynamic load, wear load, endurance 
strength of tooth, surface durability, heat dissipation – lubrication of 
gears – Merits and demerits of each type of gears. Design of spur gear 
and helical gear. 
Suggestion- discipline project- students will explore the design and 
analysis of gear systems, focusing on both spur gears and helical 
gears. The project will involve studying gear classification, 
nomenclature, tooth profiles, materials selection, and gear failure 
9 

 
 
modes. Students will apply theoretical concepts such as the Law of 
Gearing, virtual number of teeth, and gear tooth strength calculations. 
4 
Clutches – friction clutches, design considerations, multiple disc 
clutches, cone clutch, centrifugal clutch. Brakes - Block brakes, band 
brake, Internal expanding shoe brake. 
Design of Internal combustion engine parts- Piston, Cylinder, 
Connecting rod and Flywheel. 
Suggestion – discipline project- students will explore various aspects 
of clutch systems, integrating knowledge from clutches, brakes, and 
the design of internal combustion engine parts. The project will 
involve both theoretical exploration and practical application, aligning 
with the discipline Project model where students have the freedom to 
choose specific aspects to explore within the defined theme. 
 
9

SEMESTER S6 
DESIGN THINKING AND PRODUCT DEVELOPMENT 
(Common to Group C & Group D) 
Course Code 
GZEST605 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
2:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
2 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To guide students through the iterative stages of design thinking, including empathizing with 
users, defining problems, ideating solutions and developing Proof of Concepts (PoC) and 
technical feasibility studies. 
2. To promote the development of critical thinking skills by engaging students in integrative 
inquiry, where they ask meaningful questions that connect classroom knowledge with real-
world applications. 
3. To equip students with the ability to involve in product design considering the sustainability, 
inclusivity, diversity and equity aspects. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Fundamentals of design thinking and product development: Overview of 
stages of product development lifecycle; Design thinking -Definition-Design 
thinking for product innovation; Bringing social impact in ideation-Identifying 
societal needs-understanding multi-faceted issues-community engagement 
and empathetic design- technological innovation meeting societal needs; 
Understanding and Bridging the divide using Human Centered Design (HCD); 
Designing for inclusivity in product development-embracing user diversity - 
Long term impact - sustainability encompassing environmental,economic and 
social dimensions; Technology Readiness Level in the Innovation Life-cycle; 
Performing a self-check on innovative ideas - Originality of idea- 
understanding innovation landscape - patentability - understanding the 
6 

 
 
economic landscape - Unique Selling Proposition (USP) - Repeatability and 
Manufacturability - Sustainability - Leveraging business models for 
comprehensive analysis 
2 
Empathize: Design thinking phases; Role of empathy in design thinking; 
Methods of empathize phase - Ask 5 Why/ 5 W+H questions;  Empathy maps 
-  Things to be done prior to empathy mapping - Activities during and after 
the session; Understanding empathy tools - Customer Journey Map - Personas. 
Define: Methods of Define Phase: Storytelling, Critical items diagrams, 
Define success. 
6 
3 
Ideation : Stages of ideation; Techniques and tools - Divergent thinking tools 
- Convergent thinking tools - Idea capturing tools; Cross-industry inspiration; 
Role of research in ideation - Market research - consumer research - leveraging 
research for informed ideation; Technological trends - navigating the 
technological landscape - Integrating emerging technologies; Feasibility 
studies - technical, economic, market, operational, legal,  and ethical 
feasibility; Ideation session- techniques and tips. 
Proof of Concept (PoC) : Setting objectives; Risk assessment; Technology 
scouting; Document and process management; Change management; 
Knowledge Capture; Validating PoC; Story telling in PoC presentation 
6 
4 
Design: Navigating from PoC to detailed design; Developing Specification 
Requirement Document (SRD); Design for manufacturability; Design to cost; 
Pre-compliance; Design Failure Mode and Effects Analysis (DFMEA); 
Forecasting future design changes. 
Prototyping: Alpha prototypes; Beta prototypes; Transition from design to 
prototype; Goals and expectations for Alpha and Beta prototypes; Effective 
strategies for maintaining timeline in prototyping; Testing and refining Alpha 
prototypes; Transitioning to Beta prototypes. 
Pilot build: Definition and purpose of a pilot build; setting objectives; 
Identification and selection of manufacturing partner for pilot build; Testing 
procedures in pilot build; Scaling from pilot build to full-scale production / 
implementation. 
6

Sample Assignments: 
1. Evaluate and prepare a report on how the aspects including inclusivity, diversity and equity are taken 
into consideration during the empathize and define phases of the Miniproject course. 
2. Evaluate and prepare a report on how the aspects including sustainability, inclusivity, diversity and 
equity are taken into consideration during the ideate phase of the Miniproject course. 
3. Evaluate and prepare a report on how User-Centric Design (UCD) is used in the design and development 
of PoC of the product being developed in the Miniproject course. 
4. Prepare a plan for the prototype building of the product being developed in the Miniproject course. 
5. Report on the activities during the empathize phase including the maps & other materials created during 
the sessions. 
6. Report on the activities during the define phase including the maps & other materials created during the 
sessions.

AUTOMATED GUIDED AND AUTONOMOUS VEHICLES    
Course Code 
OEMUT611  
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand the principles and components of AGV and autonomous vehicle technologies. 
2. To explore the various sensor technologies and their integration into AGV and autonomous 
systems. 
3. To analyse the role of AI, machine learning, and software platforms in AGV and autonomous 
driving 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Fundamentals of Autonomous Driving - Levels of vehicle autonomy (SAE 
levels 0-5), Key components of autonomous vehicles, Overview of 
autonomous vehicle architectures  
Automated Guided Vehicles (AGV) Overview - Definition and applications 
of AGVs, Types of AGVs: Tugger, Unit Load, Forklift, Key components of 
AGVs 
Vehicle Communication and Networking - In-vehicle networking (CAN, LIN, 
FlexRay), Vehicle-to-everything (V2X) communication, Role of wireless 
technology in autonomous driving 
Regulatory and Ethical Considerations- Legal aspects of autonomous driving, 
Ethical considerations and safety standards, Current regulations and future 
trends 
 
9 
2 
Radar and Lidar Systems - Basics of radar technology, Applications and 
limitations of radar in vehicles, Fundamentals of Lidar technology, Lidar 
 
 

 
 
applications in 3D mapping and obstacle detection 
Camera Systems and Image Processing - Types of cameras used in ADAS 
and AGVs, Image processing techniques for vehicle safety, Night vision 
technology and applications 
Ultrasonic and Infrared Sensors - Principles of ultrasonic sensor operation, 
Applications in parking assist and obstacle detection 
Infrared sensors and their role in ADAS and AGVs 
Sensor Data Fusion - Introduction to sensor data fusion, Techniques for 
combining data from different sensors, Benefits of sensor fusion in enhancing 
system accuracy and reliability 
 
 
 
 
 
 
9 
3 
Artificial Intelligence and Machine Learning - Role of AI in autonomous 
vehicles and AGVs, Machine learning algorithms for vehicle perception and 
decision-making, Deep learning applications in autonomous driving 
Autonomous Driving Platforms and Software - Overview of autonomous 
driving software architectures, Key platforms: ROS (Robot Operating 
System), Autoware, Apollo, Software development and simulation tools 
Path Planning and Control Systems - Fundamentals of path planning 
algorithms, Control systems for vehicle stability and navigation, Real-time 
decision-making and obstacle avoidance 
Cloud Computing and Edge Processing - Role of cloud computing in 
autonomous vehicle ecosystems, Edge processing for real-time data handling, 
Examples of cloud-based autonomous driving platforms 
9 
4 
System Integration and Calibration - Integration of ADAS and AGV 
components into vehicle systems, Calibration techniques for sensors and 
actuators, Challenges in system integration 
Testing and Validation -   testing methodologies for autonomous and AGV 
systems, Simulation environments and test tracks, Validation processes and 
safety assessments 
Maintenance and Troubleshooting - Common issues in ADAS, AGV, and 
autonomous systems, Diagnostic tools and software, Maintenance best 
practices for autonomous vehicles and AGVs 
Case studies of leading autonomous vehicle and AGV projects, Emerging 
trends in autonomous driving and AGV technology 
 
9

SEMESTER S6 
MODERN AUTOMOTIVE TECHNOLOGIES 
Course Code 
OEMUT612 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand the modern technologies automotive technologies like Electric, hybrid and fuel cell 
vehicle technology, different components associated with these systems. 
2. To understand the various ADAS technologies such as adaptive cruise control, lane-keeping 
assist, and automated parking systems. 
3. To understand the automobile navigation systems, connected vehicles and autonomous driving 
cars. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Electric and Hybrid Vehicle technology: Introduction, LEV, TLEV, 
ULV & ZEV, Basic components of Electric vehicles- Inverters, Battery 
packs and battery management system, motors, electronic power 
control unit, Electric wiring harness – CAN Bus, Multiplex wiring. 
regenerative braking, basic factors to be considered for converting 
automobiles to electric vehicle, hybrid electric vehicle, types - series 
and parallel hybrid, layouts, comparison, Power systems and control 
systems, Different modes of operation of hybrid vehicles for best 
performance. 
9 
2 
Recent Trends in Automotive Power Plants: Stratified charged / lean 
burn engines – TSI engines, RCCI engines, Hydrogen Engines, Flex 
fuel vehicles. Vehicle Operation and engine Control: Application of 
sensors and actuators and microprocessors for operation of the vehicle 
9 

 
 
to achieve best fuel economy, reduced emission and optimum road 
performance, Closed loop and open loop operation, electronic engine 
management systems, Electronic cruise control, chassis control 
system, Integrated systems. 
3 
Principle of automobile navigation and controls in the new generation 
cars- capabilities of navigation and control of modern cars. Driver 
Assistance Systems in Automobiles: Vision in cars, A comprehensive 
driver assistance approach – Lane recognition, Traffic sign recognition, 
road recognition, Object recognition – Traffic lights and signals. 
9 
4 
Fuel Cells and Alternative energy systems: Introduction to fuel cells, 
Operational fuel cell voltages, Proton Exchange membrane fuel cells, 
Alkaline Electrolyte fuel cells, Medium and high temperature fuel cells, 
fuel and fuel chose, fuel processing, fuel cell stacks, Delivering fuel cell 
power, Integrated Air supply and humidification concepts for fuel cell 
systems, Fuel cell Auxiliary systems. 
9

SEMESTER S6 
SPECIAL TYPES OF VEHICLES   
Course Code 
OEMUT614  
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Comprehend the design and functionality of various special types of vehicles, including 
their unique features and applications. 
2. Analyse the operational principles and maintenance requirements of special vehicles 
used in different industries. 
3. Develop problem-solving skills for troubleshooting and optimizing the performance of 
special types of vehicles. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Tyre and tracked vehicles, advantages and disadvantages, undercarriage 
of tracked vehicle - tracks, roller frames, drive sprockets, track rollers, 
track chains and track shoes. Suspension and steering of tyre and 
tracked vehicle             
 Final drives: types of reductions like, single reduction, double 
reduction final drive and planetary final drives, PTO shaft, Basic 
components of hydraulic systems like pumps (types of pumps), control 
valves like flow control valves, directional control valves and pressure 
control valves, hydraulic motors and hydraulic cylinders. 
 
9 
2 
Tractors: General description, specification and functions, light, 
medium and heavy wheeled tractors, crawler tracks mounted / wheeled-
bulldozers, tilt dozers and angle dozers, front end loaders, Productivity 
& operating capacity of dozer. 
 
9 

 
 
Excavators: General description, classification based on attachments, 
face shovel, drag shovel, hoe, drag-line and grab or clam shell, 
advantages and limitations. 
3 
Haulage vehicles: General description, specification and functions, self-
propelled and tractor towed haulage vehicles, dumpers – front tipping; 
trucks – rear tipping, tractor towed semi-trailers and trailers (rear and 
side tipping, bottom dumping).  
Graders: Description, classification and functions of graders, functional 
details of spreading, mixing, ditching, bank sloping, snow removal, 
stripping, scarifying, and finishing. 
Scrapers: General description, classification- tractor towed and 
motorized scrapers, scraper loading – back track and chain track 
loading, operations - scraper work in cutting, cambering, side hill 
cutting, spreading on embankments 
9 
4 
Cranes: General description, specifications and functions, excavator 
mounted cranes, mobile cranes with strut and cantilever type jibs, 
tractor towed and tractor mounted cranes. Lift trucks: General 
description, specification and functions, fork lift trucks, alternative front 
end equipment (attachments) – jib arm, shovel bucket, squeeze clamp, 
boom, fork extensions, barrel forks. Scissors lift trucks - applications in 
industry, advantages and disadvantages. 
Compaction vehicles: General description, specification and functions, 
smooth wheeled rollers, pneumatic tired rollers, agricultural Rollers, 
sheep’s foot rollers; vibrating compactors. 
 
9

SEMESTER: S6 
AUTOTRONICS LAB 
Course Code 
PCAUL607 
CIE Marks 
50 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
0:0:3:0 
ESE Marks   
50 
Credits 
2 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Lab 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To provide students with hands-on experience in inspecting, servicing on various electronics 
circuits associated with automobiles. 
2. To equip students with the practical skills necessary for diagnosing, maintaining, and adjusting 
electronics associated with automobiles. 
3. To enable students to proficiently perform and interpret diagnostic tests and measurements, using 
advanced technological systems for electronic systems. 
 
Expt.  
No. 
Experiments 
1 
Testing of various sensors used in automobiles. 
2 
Testing and validation of logic gate ICs using ARDUINO. 
3 
Testing and validation of flip flops using ARDUINO. 
4 
Testing of Diodes, Transistor, Op-amps, Relays in automotive electronic circuits. 
5 
Testing and validation of flip flops. 
6 
Programming and interfacing of Microcontrollers/Microprocessors 
7 
Interfacing of AC/DC converter, stepper motor and dc motor. 
8 
Advanced On-board diagnostics (OBD) and fault detection in electronics circuits. 
9 
Familiarization of engine remapping tools and software 
10 
Design and testing of the circuit for keyless entry, parking system. 
11 
Design and testing of the circuits for ABS, EBD and Traction Control. 
12 
Design and testing of circuit for electronic triggering equipment 
13 
MAT lab simulation for various electronic circuits (RLC circuit) 
14 
Study and testing of steer by wire technology. 
15 
Testing of NVH levels of an automobile. 

 
 
Note:- A Minimum of 12 Experiments is necessary.

16

Course Outcome 
Bloom’s 
Knowledge

K1

applications.
 
K1

for microcontrollers/microprocessors and their applications in 
automotive systems. 
 
K2 
CO4

remapping tools.
 
K2

regenerative braking, and vehicle telematics.

Video Links (NPTEL, SWAYAM…) 
 
Link ID 
 
Programming and interfacing of Microcontrollers/Microprocessors.;
https://youtu.be/MqWeH3zp5GY 
Testing and validation of electric vehicle powertrains including motors, controllers, and power 
electronics. :  https://youtu.be/gDOnBwjF55U 
 
Continuous Assessment (25 Marks) 
1. Preparation and Pre-Lab Work (7 Marks) 
 Pre-Lab Assignments: Assessment of pre-lab assignments or quizzes that test understanding 
of the upcoming experiment. 
 Understanding of Theory: Evaluation based on students’ preparation and understanding of 
the theoretical background related to the experiments. 
2. Conduct of Experiments (7 Marks) 
 Procedure and Execution: Adherence to correct procedures, accurate execution of 
experiments, and following safety protocols. 
 Skill Proficiency: Proficiency in handling equipment, accuracy in observations, and 
troubleshooting skills during the experiments. 
 Teamwork: Collaboration and participation in group experiments. 
3. Lab Reports and Record Keeping (6 Marks) 
 Quality of Reports: Clarity, completeness and accuracy of lab reports. Proper documentation 
of experiments, data analysis and conclusions. 

 
 
 Timely Submission: Adhering to deadlines for submitting lab reports/rough record and 
maintaining a well-organized fair record. 
 
4. Viva Voce (5 Marks) 
 Oral Examination: Ability to explain the experiment, results and underlying principles 
during a viva voce session. 
Final Marks Averaging: The final marks for preparation, conduct of experiments, viva, and 
record are the average of all the specified experiments in the syllabus. 
Evaluation Pattern for End Semester Examination (50 Marks) 
1. Procedure/Preliminary Work/Design/Algorithm (10 Marks) 
 Procedure Understanding and Description: Clarity in explaining the procedure and 
understanding each step involved. 
 Preliminary Work and Planning: Thoroughness in planning and organizing 
materials/equipment. 
 Algorithm Development: Correctness and efficiency of the algorithm related to the 
experiment. 
 Creativity and logic in algorithm or experimental design. 
 
2. Conduct of Experiment/Execution of Work/Programming (15 Marks) 
 Setup and Execution: Proper setup and accurate execution of the experiment or programming 
task. 
3. Result with Valid Inference/Quality of Output (10 Marks) 
 Accuracy of Results: Precision and correctness of the obtained results. 
 Analysis and Interpretation: Validity of inferences drawn from the experiment or quality of 
program output. 
 
4. Viva Voce (10 Marks) 
 Ability to explain the experiment, procedure results and answer related questions 
 Proficiency in answering questions related to theoretical and practical aspects of the subject. 
5. Record (5 Marks) 
 Completeness, clarity, and accuracy of the lab record submitted

AUTOMOBILE ENGINEERING 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 

SEMESTER S7 
VEHICLE BODY ENGINEERING 
Course Code 
PEAUT741 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To provide a comprehensive understanding on vehicle body design and classification 
2. To equip students to analyse and apply materials and manufacturing techniques 
3. To introduce advanced technologies and enhance vehicle safety and aerodynamics 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to Vehicle Body Engineering: Classification of Coach Work 
type: Stylish Forms, Coach and Bus body style, layout of cars, buses and coach 
with different seating and loading capacity, Commercial vehicle types, Vans 
and Pickups 
Terms Used in Bus Body Building – Angle of Approach and Departure, 
Ground Clearance, Fender, Floor Longitudes, Post, Seat rails, Cant Rails, 
waist rails, roof sticks, Roof Longitude, Rub Rail, Skirt Rail, Wheel Arch 
Structure, Post Diagonals, Gussets, Industry standards and regulations that 
affect vehicle body design and construction 
 
9 
2 
Vehicle Body materials –Aluminium Alloys, Steel, Alloy steels, Plastics, 
metal Matrix composites, Glass reinforced plastics and high strength 
composites, Thermoplastics, ABS, Load Bearing Plastics, semi rigid PUR 
Foams and Sandwich Panel Construction, Recycling of vehicle materials and 
sustainable practices in material selection and manufacturing. 
Paints and Adhesives – Paints, Adhesives and its properties, Corrosions, and 
their prevention  
9 
3 
Vehicle Aerodynamics - Objectives, Vehicle drag and types, various types of 
forces and moments influencing drag, Effect of forces and moments, Side 
9 

wind effects on force and moments, Introduction to CFD tools used in the 
design process for aerodynamic analysis. 
Various body optimization – Techniques for minimum drag, Wind Tunnels- 
Types and Principles, Flow Visualization techniques, Airflow Management 
System 
4 
Vehicle Safety - Passive and Active vehicle Safety equipment’s – Seat belt, 
Collapsible steering column, tilt able steering wheel, Air Bags, Electronic 
system for activating Air bag, Impact of emerging technologies such as 
electric vehicles (EVs) and Autonomous vehicles on vehicle body 
engineering. 
9

SEMESTER S7 
TOTAL QUALITY MANAGEMENT 
Course Code 
PEAUT742 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To equip students with foundational and advanced knowledge in Total Quality Management 
(TQM), including quality evaluation 
2. To introduce students about leadership strategies, practical improvement tools, and advanced 
quality techniques for enhancing organizational performance. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction - Need for Quality – Evaluation of Quality – Definitions of 
Quality – Dimensions of product and service quality – Basic concepts of TQM 
– TQM frame work – Contributions of Deming, Juran, and Crossby – Barriers 
of TQM – Quality statements – Customer focus – Customer orientation, 
Customer satisfaction, Customer complaints – Customer retention – Costs of 
Quality.  International quality standards - ISO 9001, ISO/TS 16949, and their 
significance in the global market. 
 
9 
2 
Leadership - Strategic quality planning, Quality Councils - Employee 
involvement - Motivation, Empowerment, Team and Teamwork, Quality 
circles Recognition and Reward, Performance appraisal - Continuous process 
improvement PDCA cycle, 5S, Kaizen Supplier partnership - Partnering, 
Supplier selection, Supplier Rating. Change management in implementing 
TQM practices within an organization. 
9 
3 
The seven traditional tools of quality - New management tools - Six sigma: 
Concepts, Methodology, applications to manufacturing, service sector 
including IT-Bench marking -Reason to bench mark, Bench marking process 
9 

– FMEA - Stages, Types, Integration of lean manufacturing principles with 
TQM, Fishbone Diagram (Ishikawa), Design of Experiments (DOE) 
4 
Control Charts - Process Capability - Concepts of Six Sigma - Quality 
Function Development (QFD) - Taguchi quality loss function -TPM - 
Concepts, improvement needs - Performance measures.  
Case Studies related to TQM in the automotive industry, impact of Industry 
4.0 and AI on quality management processes. Ethics in Quality Management.
9

SEMESTER S7 
ADVANCED AUTOMOTIVE MANUFACTURING MATERIALS 
Course Code 
PEAUT745 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
5/3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand the fundamental properties of various materials used in automotive 
manufacturing, such as metals, polymers, composites, and ceramics.  
2. To understand the latest advancements in automotive materials, including lightweight 
materials, high-strength alloys, and smart materials. 
3. To understand the environmental impact of material selection and manufacturing processes in 
the automotive industry. 
4. To Understand the emerging trends in automotive materials, including electric vehicle 
materials, light weighting for fuel efficiency, and advancements in battery technology 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to Automotive Materials: Overview of material types: metals, 
polymers, composites, and ceramics. Criteria for material selection in the 
automotive industry.  Metals in Automotive Applications; Ferrous and non-
ferrous alloys. Properties Polymers and Composites, Thermoplastics, 
thermosetting plastics, and elastomers. Reinforced plastics, carbon fibre 
composites, and their automotive applications. Applications of steel, 
aluminium, magnesium, and titanium alloys. Ceramics and Glass. Structural 
ceramics, advanced ceramics, and their uses in engines and braking systems. 
Glass materials: properties and applications in automotive glazing. 
 
9 
2 
Lightweight Materials: Importance of weight reduction in automotive design. 
Applications of advanced high-strength steels (AHSS), aluminium alloys, and 
magnesium alloys. High-Performance Materials, Superalloys, titanium alloys, 
and their applications in high-performance vehicles. Introduction to smart 
9 

materials and shape memory alloys.  Surface Engineering and Coatings 
Surface treatments, coatings for corrosion resistance, and wear protection. 
Role of coatings in improving material performance and longevity.  Additive 
Manufacturing and Nanotechnology: Overview of additive manufacturing 
processes and their applications in the automotive industry. Nanomaterials: 
properties, synthesis, and applications. 
3 
Environmental Considerations in Material Selection: Life cycle assessment 
(LCA) of automotive materials. Impact of materials on vehicle emissions and 
fuel efficiency. Strategies for recycling metals, polymers, and composites. 
End-of-life vehicle (ELV) recycling and circular economy concepts. 
Development and application of bio-based and biodegradable materials. Eco-
design principles and their implementation in automotive manufacturing. 
Overview of environmental regulations affecting the automotive industry. 
Standards for automotive material sustainability and compliance. 
9 
4 
Materials for Electric Vehicles (EVs): Requirements for light weighting and 
energy efficiency in EVs. Battery materials: lithium-ion, solid-state batteries, 
and future alternatives. Advanced Materials for Fuel Efficiency: 
Aerodynamics, lightweight materials, and their role in reducing fuel 
consumption, Use of composites and advanced alloys in structural 
components.  Smart and Functional Materials: Development of self-healing 
materials, sensors, and conductive materials for automotive applications. 
Integration of smart materials in vehicle systems and components. Future 
Directions in Automotive Materials: Trends in material innovation, 
sustainability, and manufacturing processes. Research and development 
opportunities in new materials and technologies. 
9 
 
Course Assessment Method 
(CIE: 40 marks, ESE: 60 marks) 
 
 
Continuous Internal Evaluation Marks (CIE): 
 
Attendance 
Internal Ex 
Evaluate  
Analyse 
Total 
5 
15 
10 
10 
40 
 
Assignment: 20 Marks 
Students should evaluate and analyze a real-world optimization problem, assess the proposed solutions, 
provide a conclusion on which solution is most appropriate for the problem, and implement the chosen 
solution using any specific technique/tool/software/programme.  
 

Criteria for evaluation: 
1. Problem Definition (K4 - 4 points) 
a. Clearly defines the real-world optimization problem. 
b. Examine and identifies relevant contextual factors (constraints, resources, objectives). 
2. Problem Analysis (K4 - 4 points) 
a. Break-down and presents a well-reasoned solution approach. 
b. Compare and justify the proposed solutions with evidence and logical reasoning. 
3. Evaluate (K5 - 4 points) 
a. Thoroughly evaluate the proposed solutions. 
b. Compares trade-offs, advantages, and disadvantages. 
c. Considers feasibility, scalability, and practical implications. 
4. Implementation (K5 - 4 points) 
a. Select the most feasible solution by implementing the proposed solutions/techniques. 
b. Successfully translates the problem to solution using proposed technique. 
c. Demonstrates proficiency in solution practices (readability, efficiency, error handling). 
5. Conclusion (K4- 2 points, K5 – 2 points) 
a. Summarizes findings and insights. State which solution is most appropriate for the problem. 
(K4) 
b. Reflects critical thinking and informed decision-making. (K5) 
Scoring: 
1. Accomplished (4 points): Exceptional analysis, clear implementation, and depth of 
understanding. 
2. Competent (3 points): Solid performance with minor areas for improvement. 
3. Developing (2 points): Adequate effort but lacks depth or clarity. 
4. Minimal (1 point): Incomplete or significantly flawed.

SEMESTER S7 
BLOCK CHAIN IN AUTOMOTIVE INDUSTRY 
Course Code 
PEAUT751 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
NA 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To introduce the fundamentals of blockchain technology and its relevance to the automotive 
industry. 
2. To explore the potential applications of blockchain in various aspects of the automotive sector, 
including supply chain, manufacturing, and vehicle maintenance. 
3. To equip students with the knowledge to analyze and implement blockchain solutions in 
automotive engineering contexts. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Fundamentals of blockchain technology, how blockchain works: blocks, 
chains, nodes, and networks, Key concepts: decentralization, consensus 
mechanisms -Purpose of consensus in blockchain, Types of consensus 
mechanisms: (basic ideas only), Types of blockchains: public, private, and 
consortium, Overview of cryptocurrencies and their relation to blockchain 
9 
2 
Use cases of blockchain in automotive supply chain management, Blockchain 
for vehicle manufacturing and assembly processes, Enhancing transparency 
and traceability in automotive logistics, Blockchain for quality assurance and 
compliance in automotive manufacturing, Case studies of blockchain 
implementation in leading automotive companies 
9 
3 
Digital vehicle identities and smart contracts, Blockchain for vehicle 
registration and ownership transfer, Securing vehicle data and maintenance 
9 

history with blockchain, Role of blockchain in vehicle insurance and claims 
processing, Practical applications, and case studies 
4 
Emerging trends in blockchain technology and their potential impact on the 
automotive industry, Challenges in adopting blockchain in automotive 
applications, Regulatory and legal considerations, Integrating blockchain with 
other technologies: IoT, AI, and big data in autonomous vehicles. Prospects 
and career opportunities in blockchain for automotive engineers 
9

SEMESTER S7 
VEHICLE AERODYNAMICS 
Course Code 
PEAUT752 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
NA 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. The course will impart knowledge of aerodynamic fundamentals and their effects on vehicle 
performance.  
2. To introduce aerodynamic testing using wind tunnel testing, CFD, with the relative merits and 
limitations. 
3. To enhance aerodynamic design for various vehicles. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to Aerodynamics-Concept of Fluids, Basic Fluid Mechanics- 
Fluid properties related to aerodynamics, Forces in a fluid, Compressibility 
and incompressibility, Reynolds Number (Re), Mach number, Laminar and 
turbulent flow, hypersonic flows, Boundary Layer, Flow separation, 
Streamlines Streak lines and Path lines, Flow Visualization Techniques-types 
and application 
 
9 
2 
Fundamentals of Aerodynamics- Resistances to vehicle motion.  
Aerodynamic drag, Effects of air resistance in vehicle performance and 
stability, pressure drag, Air flow wake, Relation between air resistance, frontal 
area, and vehicle velocity, drag co-efficient (simple problems related to the 
relations), Idea of drag co-efficient of various shapes.  
 
9 
3 
Aerodynamic lift and Downforce -Vehicle Handling-The origin of force and 
moments on a vehicle, Effects of forces and moments, Side wind problems, 
Vehicle dynamics Under side winds, Car body drag reduction, wind noise, 
Aerodynamic lift control- Aerodynamic aids, after body drag- square back 
 
9 

drag, fast back drag, notch back drag, hatch back drag. Effect of down force 
on vehicle performance, Vortices 
4 
Aerodynamic Testing- Wind Tunnels for Automotive, Principles of wind 
tunnel technology, Types, and components of wind tunnel. Limitation of 
simulation – Stress with scale models – Full scale wind tunnels – Measurement 
techniques – Equipment and transducers – Road testing methods, numerical 
methods-CFD. Aerodynamic study of F1 Racing cars, Sports car, SUVs. 
 
9

(CIE: 40 marks, ESE: 60 marks)

SEMESTER S7 
SUPPLY CHAIN MANAGEMENT 
Course Code 
PEAUT753 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. To provide students with a comprehensive understanding of supply chain management 
principles and their strategic importance in the automotive industry. 
2. To equip students with the skills to plan, forecast, and optimize supply chain operations, 
focusing on inventory management, production planning, and transportation. 
3. To enable students to apply collaborative strategies and emerging technologies to enhance 
supply chain integration and address challenges in a globalized environment. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to Supply Chain Management  
Overview of Supply Chain Management (SCM): Definition, importance, and 
key components of SCM in the automotive industry. Supply Chain Concepts 
and Terminology: Understanding the supply chain, logistics, value chain, and 
their interrelations. Automotive Supply Chain Structure: Components of the 
automotive supply chain, including suppliers, manufacturers, distributors, 
retailers, and customers. Supply Chain Models and Frameworks: Overview of 
common supply chain models, such as the SCOR model, and their application 
in the automotive industry. Role of SCM in the Automotive Industry: The 
strategic importance of SCM in reducing costs, improving efficiency, and 
enhancing customer satisfaction in the automotive sector. 
9 
2 
Supply Chain Planning and Strategy  
Strategic Supply Chain Planning: Long-term planning and decision-making in 
supply chain management to align with business goals. Demand Forecasting 
and Planning: Techniques for predicting customer demand and aligning 
9 

production schedules accordingly. Inventory Management: Principles of 
inventory control, optimization strategies, and their importance in the 
automotive supply chain. Production Planning and Control: Integration of 
production schedules with supply chain processes to ensure smooth 
operations. Transportation and Distribution Planning: Planning and 
optimizing the movement of goods from suppliers to customers, focusing on 
efficiency and cost-effectiveness. 
3 
Supply Chain Integration and Collaboration  
Supply Chain Integration: Strategies for achieving seamless integration of 
internal and external supply chain processes. Role of Information Technology 
in SCM: How IT systems and tools like ERP, SCM software, and IoT are used 
to enhance supply chain visibility and efficiency. Collaborative Planning, 
Forecasting, and Replenishment (CPFR): Framework for collaboration 
between supply chain partners to improve demand planning and inventory 
management. Vendor-Managed Inventory (VMI): Understanding VMI 
systems and their benefits in reducing inventory levels and improving supplier 
relationships. Case Studies in Supply Chain Collaboration: Analysis of 
successful collaboration practices in the automotive industry and lessons 
learned. 
9 
4 
Emerging Trends and Challenges in Supply Chain Management  
Globalization and Its Impact on Supply Chains: Understanding the effects of 
globalization on supply chain complexity, risk, and management practices. 
Sustainable Supply Chain Management: Strategies for implementing 
environmentally sustainable practices in the automotive supply chain. Risk 
Management in Supply Chains: Identifying and mitigating risks in the supply 
chain, including geopolitical risks, natural disasters, and supply disruptions. 
Agile supply chains, and the move towards a circular economy. Technological 
Innovations in SCM: Exploring the impact of emerging technologies; AI, 
blockchain, and big data analytics on supply chain management. 
 
9
