SEMESTER S7 
NOISE, VIBRATION AND HARSHNESS 
Course Code 
PEAUT755 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
5/3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
NA 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To impart fundamental knowledge of acoustics and vibration principles and their relevance in 
the automotive industry. 
2. To enable students to understand and analyse the sources and control methods of noise and 
vibrations in vehicles. 
3. To familiarize students with the psychological effects of noise and vibration and the standards 
and legislations related to NVH in the automotive field. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Fundamentals of Acoustics – General types of sound wave propagation, 
linearized wave equation, Acoustic velocity potential, Propagation of sound 
waves, sound intensity, energy density, sound power, Inhomogeneous wave 
equation, Lighthill’s analogy, effect of the presence of solid bodies in the flow. 
The Powell Howe theory of vortex sound. Acoustic source models, 
monopoles, dipoles, quadrupole. 
 
9 
2 
Fundamental of Vibration- Basic concept of vibration, Damped and un 
damped vibration, Free and forced vibration, Analysis of single degree 
freedom system and two-degree freedom system. Modes of vibration, 
Resonance, Transmissivity, Vibration isolation.  
9 
3 
Vibration Measurement and Control- Sources of vibration, Vibration 
pickups, Transducers, Accelerometers, Different types of dampers, Viscous 
damping, sand-witch construction, Vibration absorbers and isolators. 
Noise Measurement and Control- Sources of noise, Noise measuring 
instruments, microphones, sound intensity probes, Noise control methods, 
9 

active and semi active control of noise, anechoic chamber, isolators and noise 
absorbing materials.  
4 
Harshness- Definition, psychological effect of noise and vibration, sound 
quality matric, loudness, roughness, sharpness, fluctuation strength, 
psychoacoustic indexes, acceptable degree of harshness, Sound quality 
indexes for high frequency tonal noise, Application of sound quality indexes 
in NVH analysis, Study of NVH legislations applicable for vehicles in India, 
Introduction to software applications for NVH analysis. 
9 
Course Assessment Method 
(CIE: 40 marks, ESE: 60 marks) 
 
Continuous Internal Evaluation Marks (CIE): 
 
Attendance 
Internal Ex 
Evaluate  
Analyse 
Total 
5 
15 
10 
10 
40 
 
Assignment: 20 Marks 
Students should evaluate and analyze a real-world optimization problem, assess the proposed solutions, 
provide a conclusion on which solution is most appropriate for the problem, and implement the chosen 
solution using any specific technique/tool/software/programme.  
 
Criteria for evaluation: 
6. Problem Definition (K4 - 4 points) 
a. Clearly defines the real-world optimization problem. 
b. Examine and identifies relevant contextual factors (constraints, resources, objectives). 
7. Problem Analysis (K4 - 4 points) 
a. Break-down and presents a well-reasoned solution approach. 
b. Compare and justify the proposed solutions with evidence and logical reasoning. 
8. Evaluate (K5 - 4 points) 
a. Thoroughly evaluate the proposed solutions. 
b. Compares trade-offs, advantages, and disadvantages. 
c. Considers feasibility, scalability, and practical implications. 
9. Implementation (K5 - 4 points) 
a. Select the most feasible solution by implementing the proposed solutions/techniques. 
b. Successfully translates the problem to solution using proposed technique. 
c. Demonstrates proficiency in solution practices (readability, efficiency, error handling). 
10. Conclusion (K4- 2 points, K5 – 2 points) 
a. Summarizes findings and insights. State which solution is most appropriate for the problem. 
(K4) 
b. Reflects critical thinking and informed decision-making. (K5) 

Scoring: 
5. Accomplished (4 points): Exceptional analysis, clear implementation, and depth of 
understanding. 
6. Competent (3 points): Solid performance with minor areas for improvement. 
7. Developing (2 points): Adequate effort but lacks depth or clarity. 
8. Minimal (1 point): Incomplete or significantly flawed.

SEMESTER S7 
ELECTRIC AND HYBRID VEHICLE 
Course Code 
OEMUT721 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60

Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Understand the fundamental principles and components of Electric and Hybrid vehicle 
technologies, including their energy conversion mechanisms and powertrain configurations.
 
 
2. Understand the environmental and societal impacts of Electric and Hybid vehicles, comparing 
their advantages and challenges with conventional internal combustion engine vehicles. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Introduction to Electric vehicles: Past, Present & Future of EV, Current 
Major Issues, Recent Development Trends, EV Concept, Key EV Technology, 
State-of-the Art EVs & HEVs, Comparison of EV Vs IC Engine. EV System: 
EV Configuration: Fixed & variable gearing, single & multiple motor drive, 
In-wheel drives EV Parameters: Weight, size, force, energy & performance 
parameters. 
 
9 
2 
Introduction to hybrid vehicles: Need for hybrid and electric vehicles, 
components, advantages and disadvantages, application, social and 
environmental impacts. Hybrid Electric Drive-trains: Basic concept of hybrid 
traction, introduction to various hybrid drive-train topologies (Series, Parallel, 
Series – Parallel), power flow control in hybrid drive-train topologies 
9 
3 
Electric Machines and their controllers: ‘Brushed’ DC Electric Motor - 
DC regulation and voltage conversion; Brushless Electric Motors - 
Brushless DC motor, Switched reluctance motors, Induction motor; Motor 
cooling, efficiency, size and mass. Thermal Management of HEV Power 
9 

Electronics 
Sizing the drive system: Matching the electric machine and the internal 
combustion engine (ICE) 
4 
Energy Storage: Introduction to Energy Storage Requirements in Hybrid and 
Electric Vehicles, Battery based energy storage and its analysis, Super 
Capacitor based energy storage and its analysis, Ultra capacitors, Flywheel 
based 
energy 
storage 
and 
its 
analysis, 
Flywheel 
Accumulators, 
Superconducting magnetic energy storage; Hydraulic Accumulators; 
Hydraulic Pumps/Motors - Pneumatic Hybrid Engine Systems. Energy 
management strategies used in hybrid and electric vehicles: types, comparison 
and implementation issues Hybridization of different energy storage devices, 
Fuel Cell technology. 
9

SEMESTER S7 
AUTOMOTIVE ERGONOMICS AND SAFETY 
Course Code 
OEMUT722 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To gain knowledge of human anatomy and anthropometric data, focusing on how these factors 
influence vehicle design to accommodate diverse populations. 
2. To apply ergonomic principles to improve comfort and safety in automotive design, considering 
the physical and psychological needs of drivers and passengers. 
3. To explore the use of ergonomic data and standards to optimize the design of advanced driving 
systems, ensuring accessibility and usability for a wide range of users. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to ergonomics: Definition and importance of ergonomics, 
History, and evolution of ergonomics in automotive design, Human anatomy 
and biomechanics, Human capabilities and limitations, Interaction between 
driver, vehicle, and environment.   
Anthropometry and Ergonomics - Body measurements and vehicle 
accommodation, Design for diverse populations (age, gender, size), 
Ergonomic considerations for special needs, Applying anthropometry data, 
Design guidelines and standards (ISO, SAE) 
 
9 
2 
Driver and Passenger Comfort - Seating Comfort, Seat design and 
adjustments, Cushion materials and support, Pressure distribution and fatigue 
reduction, Climate Control and Acoustics, HVAC systems and airflow, Noise, 
vibration, and harshness (NVH) control, Acoustic materials and insulation, 
Interior Layout and Space Utilization, Cabin space optimization, Storage and 
accessibility, Ergonomic layout of the cockpit 
9 

3 
Safety and Ergonomics- Introduction to safety: Design of the body for safety, 
energy equation, engine location, concept of crumble zone. Active and Passive 
Safety Systems, Seat belts and airbag systems, Ergonomics of dashboard and 
instrument panel, Emergency controls and their accessibility. Ergonomics in 
Advanced Driver Assistance Systems (ADAS), User-friendly interfaces for 
ADAS, Haptic feedback and tactile controls. 
9 
4 
Ergonomics in Crash Safety-Crash test dummies and ergonomic data, Vehicle 
interior design for impact protection, Innovations in Automotive Ergonomics- 
Ergonomic simulation software and tools, Ergonomic challenges in 
autonomous vehicles, Redesigning vehicle interiors for autonomous driving, 
Ergonomics in electric and hybrid vehicles. 
9

SEMESTER S7 
VEHICLE AERODYNAMICS 
Course Code 
OEAUT723 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
NA 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To learn the key principles of aerodynamics, including drag, lift, and down force, and how these 
forces influence vehicle performance. 
2. To gain knowledge of wind tunnel testing and computational fluid dynamics (CFD), including 
their applications and limitations in aerodynamic analysis. 
3. To apply aerodynamic principles and testing techniques to optimize the design and performance 
of various types of vehicles. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to Aerodynamics-Concept of Fluids, Basic Fluid 
Mechanics- Fluid properties related to aerodynamics, Forces in a fluid, 
Compressibility and incompressibility, Reynolds Number (Re), Mach 
number, Laminar and turbulent flow, hypersonic flows Boundary 
Layer, Flow separation, Streamlines Streak lines and Path lines, Flow 
Visualization Techniques-types and application 
 
9 
2 
Fundamentals of Aerodynamics- Resistances to vehicle motion.  
Aerodynamic drag, Effects of air resistance in vehicle performance and 
stability, pressure drag, Air flow wake, Relation between air resistance, 
frontal area and vehicle velocity, drag co-efficient (simple problems 
related to the relations), Idea of drag co-efficient of various shapes.  
 
9 
3 
Aerodynamic lift and Downforce -Vehicle Handling-The origin of force 
and moments on a vehicle, Effects of forces and moments, Side wind 
problems, Vehicle dynamics Under side winds, Car body drag 
9 

reduction, wind noise, Aerodynamic lift control- Aerodynamic aids, 
after body drag- square back drag, fast back drag, notch back drag, hatch 
back drag. Effect of down force on vehicle performance, Vortices 
4 
Aerodynamic Testing- Wind Tunnels for Automotive, Principles of 
wind tunnel technology, Types and components of wind tunnel. 
Limitation of simulation – Stress with scale models – Full scale wind 
tunnels – Measurement techniques – Equipment and transducers – Road 
testing methods, numerical methods-CFD. Aerodynamic study of F1 
Racing cars, Sports car, SUVs. 
 
9

SEMESTER S8 
AUTOMOTIVE COMFORT AND SAFETY ENGINEERING 
Course Code 
PEAUT861 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R)

None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To impart the basic concepts of automotive ergonomics and automotive safety 
2. To impart the basic concepts of creating workspace for driver 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Ergonomics in vehicle design – system approach – research studies – 
engineer’s role – importance and implementing ergonomics. Anthropometry 
– Use of anthropometry – calculation of percentile value. Application of 
biomechanics in vehicle design – seat design. 
Entrance and Exit from automobiles – problems during entrance and exit – 
features and dimensions – door handles, lateral sections, body opening 
clearance, hinge angles, seat bolsters, location and material. 
 
 
 
9 
2 
Driver performance measurement – driving and non-driving tasks. 
Performance measures – types and category – range – studies – deviation from 
lateral position, steering wheel angle, velocity, task time, glance duration – 
application. Driver workload measurement – present situation – methods to 
measure – studies. 
 
 
9 
3 
Vehicle evaluation – methods of data collection and analysis – subjective 
methods – rating on a scale, paired comparison, thurstone method. 
 
 
 
9 

Application of evaluation techniques – checklists, observational studies, user 
interviews, driving simulator studies, field studies. 
Understanding users – issues and considerations – vehicle types, market 
segments, female and old drivers, geographic locations. Issue in designing 
global vehicles. 
4 
Automotive safety – passive and active safety – seatbelt-three point seatbelts 
– Airbags – types and operation – crumple zones – materials – passenger cage 
– materials  
Crash testing – Ergonomic dummies-types, components and materials used, 
application, human testing – crash worthiness – deceleration curves, square 
wave, injury tolerance, control of deceleration, pole testing, roll over testing. 
Compliance testing, component testing, in-field testing, safety ratings. 
 
 
 
9

SEMESTER S8 
ADVANCED AUTOMOTIVE ELECTRICAL AND ELECTRONIC 
SYSTEMS 
Course Code 
PEAUT862 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand the working of vehicle networks and their architecture 
2. To understand how engines are controlled digitally and the working of advanced driver assist 
systems 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Vehicle Networks and software: Vehicle network systems – Introduction; 
Network Architecture – Types; Network communication; Vehicle Networks – 
CAN, LIN, MOST, Flex Ray Protocol; Vehicle Network Diagnosis; Real time 
operating systems (RTOS) – Introduction; AUTOSAR – Introduction, System 
architecture, Software architecture. 
 
9 
2 
Automotive Communication Systems: Ethernet in Automobiles. Connected 
car – Cyber – Physical systems; Wireless sensor networks; Telematics; 
Vehicle to network (V2N), Vehicle to infrastructure (V2I), Vehicle to vehicle 
(V2V), Vehicle to cloud (V2C), Vehicle to pedestrian (V2P), Vehicle to 
device (V2D), Vehicle to grid (V2G).In Vehicle networks: Types of IVNs- 
Body, Powertrain, Chassis, and Infotainment networks 
 
9 
3 
Digital engine control systems: Electronic fuel control, engine control 
sequence, open loop and closed control, cold starting, acceleration and full 
load; enrichment, deceleration leaning, overrun fuel cut off, Idle speed control 
9 

and EGR control; Fuel injection system parameters affecting combustion, 
noise and emissions in CI engines. Pilot, main, advanced post injection and 
retarded post injection. Electronic ignition control, Ignition timing map, 
Ignition timing calculation (Initial timing, Basic advance angle, Corrective 
advance angle), spark advance correction scheme. 
4 
Advanced Driver Assistance Systems:  Adaptive Cruise control system, 
Anti-lock braking system, Traction control system, electronic brake force 
distribution, electronic stability program, Airbags, Collision avoidance radar 
warning system, Tyre pressure monitoring, Lane departure warning system, 
Night vision system.  Electronic control transmission: control of shift timing, 
control of lock up, neutral to drive squat control, engine torque control. Dual 
clutch automatic, Automated manual transmission, continuously variable 
transmission. 
GPS navigation. 
 
9

SEMESTER S8 
ADVANCED VEHICLE TECHNOLOGY 
Course Code 
PEAUT865 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
5/3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand and apply various Artificial Intelligence techniques in automotive systems, 
including machine learning, deep learning, and reinforcement learning, to enhance vehicle 
functionalities such as traffic sign recognition, driver assistance, and structural design 
improvements. 
2. To explore the integration of AI and machine learning in electric vehicles for optimizing battery 
management, energy usage, and powertrain efficiency, as well as for enhancing regenerative 
braking systems and charging infrastructure. 
3. To evaluate and implement AI-driven solutions in autonomous vehicles and vehicle maintenance, 
including predictive maintenance. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Artificial Intelligence in Automotive Applications 
Types of AI Used in Vehicles: Machine Learning, Deep Learning. Benefits, 
Challenges and Ethical Considerations Machine Learning Algorithms for 
Automotive Systems - Supervised Learning- Algorithms: Regression, 
Classification, Neural Networks, and Applications in Vehicle Systems: Traffic 
Sign Recognition, Driver Assistance. Unsupervised Learning - Algorithms: 
Clustering, Dimensionality Reduction, Applications: Anomaly Detection, 
 
9 

Feature Extraction. Reinforcement Learning - Principles of Reinforcement 
Learning  
Using AI for Structural and Aesthetic Design Improvements, AI-Driven 
Simulation Techniques for Performance Evaluation 
Robotics and Automation Enhanced by AI. 
2 
AI and ML in Electric Vehicles 
AI for Battery Management: Battery Health Monitoring: Using AI to Track 
Battery Performance and Predict Failures. Energy Management: AI 
Techniques for Optimizing Battery Usage and Charging.  AI in EV Powertrain 
Optimization: Motor Control: AI for Enhancing Electric Motor Efficiency and 
Performance. Regenerative Braking: AI for Maximizing Energy Recovery.  
Charging Infrastructure and Optimization: Smart Charging Systems: AI for 
Efficient Charging Scheduling and Load Management. Charging Network 
Optimization: AI for Planning and Managing EV Charging Stations. Examples 
of AI Implementations.  
 
9 
3 
Autonomous Vehicles 
Introduction to Autonomous Vehicles, Definition and Levels of Automation, 
Overview of Automation Levels (SAE Levels 0-5), Key Components and 
working principles. Data Processing and Decision Making, Software and 
Hardware Architecture, Safety and Cyber security Considerations, Leading 
Companies, and their Innovations 
9 
4 
AI in Vehicle Maintenance and Diagnostics  
Predictive Maintenance - AI Techniques for Predicting Failures: 
Using Data Analytics to Forecast Vehicle Maintenance Needs. Condition-
Based Monitoring: AI for Monitoring Vehicle Health in Real-Time. 
AI for Diagnostic Systems - Onboard Diagnostics: AI-Enhanced Diagnostics 
for Identifying and Resolving Issues. Remote Diagnostics: Using AI for 
Diagnosing Problems from a Distance. AI in Repair and Service - Automated 
Service Recommendations: 
AI for Providing Maintenance and Repair Suggestions, Service Automation: 
AI in Automating Diagnostic and Repair Processes. 
Examples of AI-Driven Maintenance and Diagnostics 
 
9 
 
 

Course Assessment Method 
(CIE: 40 marks, ESE: 60 marks) 
 
Continuous Internal Evaluation Marks (CIE): 
 
Attendance 
Internal Ex 
Evaluate  
Analyse 
Total 
5 
15 
10 
10 
40 
 
Assignment: 20 Marks 
Students should evaluate and analyze a real-world optimization problem, assess the proposed solutions, 
provide a conclusion on which solution is most appropriate for the problem, and implement the chosen 
solution using any specific technique/tool/software/programme.  
Criteria for evaluation: 
1. Problem Definition (K4 - 4 points) 
a. Clearly defines the real-world optimization problem. 
b. Examine and identifies relevant contextual factors (constraints, resources, objectives). 
2. Problem Analysis (K4 - 4 points) 
a. Break-down and presents a well-reasoned solution approach. 
b. Compare and justify the proposed solutions with evidence and logical reasoning. 
3. Evaluate (K5 - 4 points) 
a. Thoroughly evaluate the proposed solutions. 
b. Compares trade-offs, advantages, and disadvantages. 
c. Considers feasibility, scalability, and practical implications. 
4. Implementation (K5 - 4 points) 
a. Select the most feasible solution by implementing the proposed solutions/techniques. 
b. Successfully translates the problem to solution using proposed technique. 
c. Demonstrates proficiency in solution practices (readability, efficiency, error handling). 
5. Conclusion (K4- 2 points, K5 – 2 points) 
a. Summarizes findings and insights. State which solution is most appropriate for the problem. (K4) 
b. Reflects critical thinking and informed decision-making. (K5) 
Scoring: 
1. Accomplished (4 points): Exceptional analysis, clear implementation, and depth of understanding. 
2. Competent (3 points): Solid performance with minor areas for improvement. 
3. Developing (2 points): Adequate effort but lacks depth or clarity. 
4. Minimal (1 point): Incomplete or significantly flawed.

SEMESTER S8 
VEHICLE PERFORMANCE AND TESTING 
Course Code 
OEAUT831 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand engine and vehicle testing methods, focusing on performance, energy, and fuel 
consumption. 
2. To understand crashworthiness and perform comprehensive impact tests using advanced crash 
test techniques. 
3. To analyse aerodynamic analysis and control vehicle noise and vibration through wind tunnel 
testing and NVH techniques. 
4. To analyse ride quality and safety using vibration measurement and comprehensive wheel and 
brake performance tests. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Engine and Vehicle Testing : Basic engine parameters- Measurement of BHP 
and IHP- Engine testing on dynamometers (hydraulic, eddy current, etc.)- 
Vehicle testing on chassis dynamometers (two-wheel and four-wheel)- Vehicle 
testing lanes (side slip testers, brake testers, headlight alignment testing)- 
Engine analysers for petrol and diesel engines- Exhaust gas analysers (Orsat 
apparatus, infrared gas analysers, smoke meter)- Energy consumption tests 
(engine cooling fan, air conditioning, brake compressors)- Fuel consumption 
tests, test route selection, vehicle test speeds 
 
 
 
 
 
9 

2 
Collision and Crash Testing: Human testing, dummies- Crashworthiness- 
Pole crash testing, near crash testing- Vehicle-to-vehicle impact, side impact 
testing- Crash test sensors, sensor mounting positions- Crash test data 
acquisition- Braking distance test 
 
 
 
9 
3 
Wind Tunnel Testing and Noise, Vibration and Harshness (NVH) : Wind 
tunnel test requirements- Ground boundary simulation- Wind tunnel selection 
and Reynolds number capability- Model requirements, details, and mounting- 
Test procedure- Automotive noise criteria- Standard noise measurement 
methods- Noise inside and outside the vehicle- Sources of vehicle noise (intake 
and exhaust noise, combustion noise, mechanical noise, noise from auxiliaries, 
wind noise, transmission noise, brake squeal, structure noise)- Noise control
methods 
 
 
 
9 
4 
Ride Vibration, Body Testing, Wheels, and Braking Performance: 
Vibration measurement instruments (accelerometer and signal conditioning)- 
Dynamic cornering fatigue and dynamic radial fatigue tests (procedure)- 
Impact test (road hazard impact test for wheel and tyre assemblies, test 
procedures, failure criteria, performance criteria)- Bumpers (types of tests,
pendulum test, fixed collision barrier test procedure, performance criteria)- Air

SEMESTER S8 
HYDROGEN AND FUEL CELL VEHICLES 
Course Code 
OEMUT832 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To acquire knowledge in hydrogen and fuel cell technology, including the basic properties of 
hydrogen, how fuel cells work, and their historical development. 
2. To understand various hydrogen production methods and storage solutions, focusing on renewable 
technologies, safety considerations, and energy storage systems. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Introduction to Hydrogen and Fuel Cell Vehicles: The importance of 
hydrogen as a clean energy carrier - Basic properties of hydrogen - An 
introduction to fuel cells and how they work - Historical development of 
hydrogen fuel cell technology - Comparison between hydrogen fuel cell 
vehicles and conventional internal combustion engine vehicles - Current 
trends and the future potential of hydrogen in the transportation sector - 
Overview of global initiatives and policies promoting hydrogen fuel cell 
vehicles. 
     9  
2 
Hydrogen and Fuel cell technology: Detailed operation of Proton Exchange 
Membrane Fuel Cells (PEMFC) - Key components of a fuel cell system- 
anode, cathode, electrolyte, catalyst. 
Electrochemical reactions in fuel cells - Fuel cell efficiency and performance 
metrics - Fuel cell stack design and vehicle integration - Challenges in fuel 
cell technology, degradation and lifetime issues - Innovations in fuel cell 
     9  

materials and designs - Comparative analysis of different fuel cell 
technologies - PEMFC, Solid Oxide Fuel Cells, Alkaline Fuel Cells.  
3 
Hydrogen production methods- Steam methane reforming, electrolysis - 
Renewable hydrogen production and storage solutions (compressed gas, liquid 
hydrogen) - Safety in hydrogen handling and refuelling infrastructure - Energy 
storage in hybrid and electric vehicles, including battery-based, fuel cell-
based, supercapacitor-based, and flywheel-based systems - Hybridization of 
energy storage devices - Short-term storage systems - flywheel accumulators, 
ultra-capacitors - Energy management strategies and implementation 
challenges. 
     9  
4 
Hydrogen Fuel Cell Vehicle Performance and Optimization: Vehicle 
Performance Metrics: Analysing the performance metrics of hydrogen fuel 
cell vehicles, including acceleration, range, and efficiency. Optimization 
Techniques: Techniques for optimizing fuel cell performance, including 
calibration, and tuning of fuel cell systems for different driving conditions, 
Cost Analysis and Lifecycle Assessment: Evaluating the cost of hydrogen 
fuel cell vehicles, including production, operation, and maintenance costs, 
along with lifecycle assessment. Real-World Applications: Case studies of 
hydrogen fuel cell vehicles in different applications- passenger cars, buses, 
trucks.  
     9

SEMESTER S8 
INDUSTRIAL SAFETY ENGINEERING 
Course Code 
OEAUT833 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Mins 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To impart knowledge of various safety management principles and various safety systems  
2. To compare different hazard identification tools and choose the most appropriate based on the 
nature of industry 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Need for safety:  Safety and productivity. Definitions - Accident, injury, 
unsafe act, unsafe condition, dangerous occurrence, reportable accidents. 
Theories of accident causation. Safety organization- objectives, types, 
functions, role of management, supervisors, workmen, unions, government 
and voluntary agencies in safety. Safety policy. Safety officer-responsibilities, 
authority. Safety committee-need, types and advantages 
9 
2 
Personal protection in the work environment: Types of PPEs, personal 
protective equipment, respiratory and non-respiratory equipment. Standards 
and Best Practices for PPE Selection, Use, and Maintenance. Monitoring 
safety performance: Frequency rate, severity rate, incidence rate, activity rate. 
Housekeeping - responsibility of management and employees. Advantages of 
good housekeeping. 5 s of housekeeping. Work permit system - objectives, 
hot work and cold work permits. Typical industrial models and methodology. 
Entry into confined spaces.  
9 

3 
Safety in Electrical and Electronic Systems- National and International 
Standards for Electrical Safety in Industrial Environments. Importance of 
Grounding and Bonding in Electrical and Electronic Systems. Principles of 
Safe Design in Industrial Electronics. Managing Electromagnetic 
Interference (EMI) and Compatibility (EMC).  ESD Prevention and Control 
in Electronics Manufacturing and Assembly. Innovations in Safety 
Technology - New Technologies in Safety Engineering: Smart Sensors, 
Predictive Analytics, and Automation.  
Future Trends in Industrial Safety: AI and Machine Learning Applications. 
Case Studies. 
9 
4 
Hazard identification and analysis: Hazard and risk, types of hazards 
– classification of fire, types of fire extinguishers, fire explosion and 
toxic gas release, structure of hazard identification and risk assessment. 
Identification of hazards - inventory analysis, fire and explosion hazard 
rating of process plants, - dow fire and explosion hazard index, 
preliminary hazard analysis, hazard and operability study (HAZOP)) – 
methodology, criticality analysis, corrective action and follow-up. 
Control of chemical hazards, hazardous properties of chemicals, material 
safety data sheets (MSDS). 
Importance of Safety Documentation - Types of Safety Documents: 
Safety Procedures, Risk Assessments, Incident Reports, Record Keeping 
for Compliance and Audit , Checklist.  
9
